dict(zip(users['user_id'], users['user_type']))\ncity_type_counts = users.groupby(['city', 'user_type']).size().unstack(fill_value=0).fillna(0)\nglobal_type_counts = users['user_type'].value_counts()\n\npurchases['buyer_city'] = purchases['buyer_id'].map(user_city_map)\npurchases['buyer_type'] = purchases['buyer_id'].map(user_type_map)\npurchases = purchases.dropna(subset=['buyer_city'])\nlisting_cat = dict(zip(listings['listing_id'], listings['category_id']))\npurchases['category_id'] = purchases['listing_id'].map(listing_cat)\npurchases = purchases.dropna(subset=['category_id'])\n\ntype_cat = purchases.groupby(['buyer_type', 'category_id']).size().reset_index(name='n')\ntype_cat['rate'] = type_cat.apply(lambda r: r['n'] / global_type_counts[r['buyer_type']], axis=1)\nrate_lookup = type_cat.set_index(['buyer_type', 'category_id'])['rate'].to_dict()\n\nall_data = []\nfor cat_id in sorted(cats['category_id']):\n    global_cnt = purchases[purchases['category_id'] == cat_id].shape[0]\n    if global_cnt < 30:\n        continue\n    for city in valid_cities:\n        ci = city_type_counts.loc[city]\n        exp = sum(ci.get(ut, 0) * rate_lookup.get((ut, cat_id), 0.0) for ut in ['regular', 'business', 'verified'])\n        if exp < 2.0:\n            continue\n        actual = purchases[(purchases['buyer_city'] == city) & (purchases['category_id'] == cat_id)].shape[0]\n        ratio = actual / exp\n        all_data.append({'city': city, 'cat_id': cat_id, 'actual': actual, 'expected': exp, 'ratio': ratio})\n\ndf = pd.DataFrame(all_data)\n\nresults = {}\nfor cat_id, group in df.groupby('cat_id'):\n    group = group.sort_values('ratio')\n    cat_name = cat_name_map.get(int(cat_id), str(cat_id))\n    for _, row in group.iterrows():\n        if row['ratio'] < 0.5 and row['expected'] >= 2:\n            city = row['city']\n            if city not in results:\n                results[city] = {}\n            results[city][cat_name] = row['ratio']\n\nfinal = {}\nfor city in sorted(results.keys()):\n    cats_sorted = sorted(results[city].keys(), key=lambda c: results[city][c])\n    final[city] = cats_sorted\n\nwith open('answer.json', 'w') as f:\n    json.dump(final, f)\n\nprint(json.dumps(final, indent=2))\nprint(f'\\nCities: {len(final)}')\nprint(f'Total pairs: {sum(len(v) for v in I think the right answer should be more concise.\n\nLet me look at this from a different angle. The problem says:\n\n\"find cities where the number of transactions could be further increased using dedicated strategies (such as more notifications like 'Buy products from category <X> on our platform!'), as this, for example, is strongly suggested by activity in other cities for the same listing categories.\"\n\nI think the key insight is about SUPPLY and DEMAND balance. global_purchases_count = len(cat_purchases)\n    \n    for city in valid_cities:\n        city_listings = len(cat_listings[cat_listings['seller_city'] == city])\n        city_purchases = len(cat_purchases[cat_purchases['buyer_city'] == city])\n        \n        supply_share = city_listings / global_listings_count\n        demand_share = city_purchases / global_purchases_count\n        \n        # If supply share > demand share, there's an opportunity to boost demand\n        # The gap: supply_share / demand_share (how much more supply vs demand)\n        if demand_share > 0 and
